                     <div class="text-body W-100 Font-B-1-160" id="article-aft-text-body-88980243121" style="color:#222222;max-width:500px;">
                      <div class="body read-more-cut">
                       <div class="pre-cut" style="height:auto;margin-bottom:1.5em;">
                        <p>
                         Its 1:15am and your alarm goes off. No, youre not about to drive to the airport to catch your plane to Bucharest; youre baker Jonathan Eng, and your work day has just begun. You hit snooze for 15 minutes and then youre out the door. Especially on weekends, Ill be leaving as my neighbors are coming home, Eng told us. They usually give me very strange looks.
                        </p>
                        <p>
                         As head baker at
                         <a data-ylk="elm:itm;elmt:link;t1:a2;t2:article;t3:body;t8:6d6d6a22-4651-3ba5-8b53-ea07d487b3fb;t9:18;itc:0" href="http://superbafoodandbread.com/" target="_blank">
                          Superba Food &amp; Bread
                         </a>
                         , Eng is in charge of all the
                         <a data-ylk="elm:itm;elmt:link;t1:a2;t2:article;t3:body;t8:6d6d6a22-4651-3ba5-8b53-ea07d487b3fb;t9:18;itc:0" href="https://www.yahoo.com/food/your-first-loaf-of-bread-80280594332.html" target="_blank">
                          bread
                         </a>
                         served and sold at the warehouse-y Los Angeles space from its 7:00am to 10:00pm open hours. That means hes halfway through the job when youre pushing down the lid of your French press.
                        </p>
                        <p>
                         I love what I do, he says. Youve got to, if you have the schedule I have. Here is that schedule, in detail.
                        </p>
                        <p>
                         <em>
                          Photo credit: All,
                          <a data-ylk="elm:itm;elmt:link;t1:a2;t2:article;t3:body;t8:6d6d6a22-4651-3ba5-8b53-ea07d487b3fb;t9:18;itc:0" href="http://www.jakoblayman.com/" target="_blank">
                           Jakob Layman
                          </a>
                         </em>
                        </p>
                       </div>
                       <div class="post-cut W-100" id="post-cut" style="transition-property:none;-webkit-transition-property:none;transition-duration:10s;-webkit-transition-duration:10s;transition-timing-function:ease-in;-webkit-transition-timing-function:ease-in;overflow:hidden;max-height:999999px;max-width:500px;">
                       </div>
                      </div>
                     </div>
                    </div>
                   </div>
                   <div class="W-100">
                    <img class="Maw-100 W-100" src="https://s.yimg.com/cd/resizer/FIT_TO_WIDTH-w900/27df7a8c1d7e8880af712ef8b53b88377bf1f382.jpg"/>
                   </div>
                   <div class="Maw-100 Fl-start" style="width:305px;">
                    <div>
                     <div class="Font-A-6-130" style="color:#999999;">
                      1 / 10
                     </div>
                     <div class="Font-B-1-160" style="color:#222222;">
                      2:30 am: Arrive. I get to the restaurant while the cleaning crew is there and start shaping breakfast rolls, says Eng. He uses a scale to cut pain viennois dough, which has fermented overnight.
                     </div>
                    </div>
                   </div>
                   <div class="Cl-b Py-20">
                   </div>
                   <div class="W-100">
                    <img class="ImageLoader Maw-100 W-100" src="https://s.yimg.com/g/images/spaceball.gif" style="background-image:url(https://s.yimg.com/cd/resizer/FIT_TO_WIDTH-w900/d3f7677b425e12a4d64a6322e6bc5af0bf8180fb.jpg);"/>
                   </div>
                   <div class="Maw-100 Fl-start" style="width:305px;">
                    <div>
                     <div class="Font-A-6-130" style="color:#999999;">
                      2 / 10
                     </div>
                     <div class="Font-B-1-160" style="color:#222222;">
                      3:00 am: Assemble 24 quiches. The pastry team pre-bakes the 4 x 4 shells the night before, and Eng fills them. This one is filled with potato, piquillo peppers, oregano, and smoked paprika.
                     </div>
                    </div>
                   </div>
                   <div class="Cl-b Py-20">
                   </div>
                   <div class="W-100">
                    <img class="ImageLoader Maw-100 W-100" src="https://s.yimg.com/g/images/spaceball.gif" style="background-image:url(https://s.yimg.com/cd/resizer/FIT_TO_WIDTH-w900/6badb80de0c8473b887bca0f893b845e9e1e47b2.jpg);"/>
                   </div>
                   <div class="Maw-100 Fl-start" style="width:305px;">
                    <div>
                     <div class="Font-A-6-130" style="color:#999999;">
                      3 / 10
                     </div>
                     <div class="Font-B-1-160" style="color:#222222;">
                      3:30 am: Make pain au levain. This means 90+ loaves, because while Eng removes 45 from the retarder they fermented in overnight and then bakes them off, his colleague mixes 45 more for the next day.
                     </div>
                    </div>
                   </div>
                   <div class="Cl-b Py-20">
                   </div>
                   <div class="W-100">
                    <img class="ImageLoader Maw-100 W-100" src="https://s.yimg.com/g/images/spaceball.gif" style="background-image:url(https://s.yimg.com/cd/resizer/FIT_TO_WIDTH-w900/28168cdd9c92f57bc1a7c91fc993ce115a6bdbea.jpg);"/>
                   </div>
                   <div class="Maw-100 Fl-start" style="width:305px;">
                    <div>
                     <div class="Font-A-6-130" style="color:#999999;">
                      4 / 10
                     </div>
                     <div class="Font-B-1-160" style="color:#222222;">
                      4:00 am: Straighten up: pull quiches from the oven, reorganize cooling racks, and clean wicker baskets (and their linen linings) used to ferment dough. Meanwhile, Eng's colleague mixes baguette dough.
                     </div>
                    </div>
                   </div>
                   <div class="Cl-b Py-20">
                   </div>
                   <div class="W-100">
                    <img class="ImageLoader Maw-100 W-100" src="https://s.yimg.com/g/images/spaceball.gif" style="background-image:url(https://s.yimg.com/cd/resizer/FIT_TO_WIDTH-w900/0eb279e92cc72c92672cfec3dfc791a7ffdc066e.jpg);"/>
                   </div>
                   <div class="Maw-100 Fl-start" style="width:305px;">
                    <div>
                     <div class="Font-A-6-130" style="color:#999999;">
                      5 / 10
                     </div>
                     <div class="Font-B-1-160" style="color:#222222;">
                      4:30 am: Roman pizza dough is also retarded overnight, and Eng must shape all 9 kilos. 5:00 am: Shape baguettes. Theyre in the oven by 6:15. Engs colleague mixes Italian and sprouted wheat dough.
                     </div>
                    </div>
                   </div>
                   <div class="Cl-b Py-20">
                   </div>
                   <div class="W-100">
                    <img class="ImageLoader Maw-100 W-100" src="https://s.yimg.com/g/images/spaceball.gif" style="background-image:url(https://s.yimg.com/cd/resizer/FIT_TO_WIDTH-w900/8d8e2edefe1f1c1d5a090f04a0eff17768c9708b.jpg);"/>
                   </div>
                   <div class="Maw-100 Fl-start" style="width:305px;">
                    <div>
                     <div class="Font-A-6-130" style="color:#999999;">
                      6 / 10
                     </div>
                     <div class="Font-B-1-160" style="color:#222222;">
                      6:30 am: Sprouted wheat bread. It has now fermented for a couple hours, so Eng puts it into pan loaves and proofs it for 2 hours. Eventually, he will bake it off for hot sandwiches.
                     </div>
                    </div>
                   </div>
                   <div class="Cl-b Py-20">
                   </div>
                   <div class="W-100">
                    <img class="ImageLoader Maw-100 W-100" src="https://s.yimg.com/g/images/spaceball.gif" style="background-image:url(https://s.yimg.com/cd/resizer/FIT_TO_WIDTH-w900/caa6e07a56ea272f3d8e6c3fbb24537a6d36a7e8.jpg);"/>
                   </div>
                   <div class="Maw-100 Fl-start" style="width:305px;">
                    <div>
                     <div class="Font-A-6-130" style="color:#999999;">
                      7 / 10
                     </div>
                     <div class="Font-B-1-160" style="color:#222222;">
                      7:00 am: Eng shapes Italian dough into 40 9-inch batards, like little hoagie rolls, and proofs them. 7:30 am: Then, 24 pane francese.  Its basically like the Italians trying to copy a baguette."
                     </div>
                    </div>
                   </div>
                   <div class="Cl-b Py-20">
                   </div>
                   <div class="W-100">
                    <img class="ImageLoader Maw-100 W-100" src="https://s.yimg.com/g/images/spaceball.gif" style="background-image:url(https://s.yimg.com/cd/resizer/FIT_TO_WIDTH-w900/d72457b192a06cf58d249b9bbea9dd3efa7e2d34.jpg);"/>
                   </div>
                   <div class="Maw-100 Fl-start" style="width:305px;">
                    <div>
                     <div class="Font-A-6-130" style="color:#999999;">
                      8 / 10
                     </div>
                     <div class="Font-B-1-160" style="color:#222222;">
                      8:15 am: I relieve the oven guy so he can take his break, says Eng. He bakes off all the breads and preps the tomorrows wicker baskets with rice flour, which prevents the dough from sticking.
                     </div>
                    </div>
                   </div>
                   <div class="Cl-b Py-20">
                   </div>
                   <div class="W-100">
                    <img class="ImageLoader Maw-100 W-100" src="https://s.yimg.com/g/images/spaceball.gif" style="background-image:url(https://s.yimg.com/cd/resizer/FIT_TO_WIDTH-w900/0e906574466b7492d4079aeeaf1241e4fb206fee.jpg);"/>
                   </div>
                   <div class="Maw-100 Fl-start" style="width:305px;">
                    <div>
                     <div class="Font-A-6-130" style="color:#999999;">
                      9 / 10
                     </div>
                     <div class="Font-B-1-160" style="color:#222222;">
                      10:00 am: Prep the pizzas. Shape tomorrows pain au levain, pain viennois, and Roman pizza dough and put them in the retarder. Pull anything from the oven thats still baking.
                     </div>
                    </div>
                   </div>
                   <div class="Cl-b Py-20">
                   </div>
                   <div class="W-100">
                    <img class="ImageLoader Maw-100 W-100" src="https://s.yimg.com/g/images/spaceball.gif" style="background-image:url(https://s.yimg.com/cd/resizer/FIT_TO_WIDTH-w900/07a32d2ee65f6940e187b313a25c0a19ccd3b2a8.jpg);"/>
                   </div>
                   <div class="Maw-100 Fl-start" style="width:305px;">
                    <div>
                     <div class="Font-A-6-130" style="color:#999999;">
                      10 / 10
                     </div>
                     <div class="Font-B-1-160" style="color:#222222;">
                      10:45 Feed the cultures. Pre-scale dough for the next day. 11:45 am: Mic drop. Eng goes home, takes a nap, and tends to some work on the computer. By 5:00pm, its bedtime.
                     </div>
                    </div>
                   </div>
                   <div class="Cl-b Py-20">
                   </div>
                   <div class="Maw-100 Fl-end W-100" style="max-width:500px;">
                    <div class="polls-applet">
                    </div>

                        <span class="item-title Font-A-3-120 D-b" style="word-wrap:break-word;margin-left:175px;">
                         Wedding Registries for Food Lovers
                        </span>

Add tofu, edamame, and &#x2014; my favorite &#x2014; avocado, and you have a totally satisfying meat-free meal.&#xA0;\u003C\u002Fi\u003E\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\n\u003Cp\u003E4 cups cooked pearl or hulled barley*\u003Cbr\u003E1 &#xBD; cups shelled, organic edamame\u003Cbr\u003E2 cups wild baby arugula\u003Cbr\u003E2 blocks savory, baked, organic tofu (firm or extra-firm), cut into &#xBE;-inch cubes\u003Cbr\u003E1 ripe avocado, halved and thinly sliced\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\n\u003Cp\u003E\u003Cb\u003ELemon Tamari Dressing\u003C\u002Fb\u003E\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\n\u003Cp\u003E4 tablespoons low-sodium tamari soy sauce\u003Cbr\u003E2 tablespoons toasted sesame oil\u003Cbr\u003EJuice of 1 lemon\u003Cbr\u003E1 tablespoon dried oregano\u003Cbr\u003E1 teaspoon finely grated lemon zest (optional)\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\n\u003Cp\u003EIn a large bowl, whisk together the tamari soy sauce, sesame oil, lemon juice, oregano, and lemon zest until well combined. Add slightly cooled cooked barley to the bowl and toss to coat.\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\n\u003Cp\u003EAdd the shelled edamame and arugula and toss gently to combine. To serve, divide the barley salad among four bowls and top with tofu and avocado slices.\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\n\u003Cp\u003E*Hulled barley is barley in its most natural state, which means it needs to cook for quite a bit longer than pearl barley &#x2014;1 to 1 &#xBD; hours longer. Pearl barley has the hull removed and is therefore less tough. Adjust your cooking time based on the variety you Meal Kits Help Small Farmers Find New Ways to Distribute Food?","summary":"A horde of new, sleek, venture capital-funded services has arrived on the market peddling what they think is a solution: kits made of raw ingredients  portioned and sometimes prepped  that can be assembled quickly to make a meal from scratch.","body":"\u003Cfigure class=\"tmblr-full\"\u003E\n \u003Cimg src=\"https:\u002F\u002Fs.yimg.com\u002Fcd\u002Fresizer\u002F2.0\u002FFIT_TO_WIDTH-w540\u002Fcf2d8a67b35ba526e60d2561d5701207687368a6.jpg\" alt=\"Can Meal Kits Help Small Farmers Find New Ways to Distribute Food?\" width=\"540\" height=\"360\"\u003E\n\u003C\u002Ffigure\u003E\n\u003Cp\u003E\u003Ci\u003EA tamale kit from Luke&#x2019;s Local.\u003C\u002Fi\u003E\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\n\u003Cp\u003E\u003Ci\u003EBy Anna Roth, Civil Eats\u003C\u002Fi\u003E\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\n\u003Cp\u003EPutting food on the table on a busy weeknight is a universal problem. Now, a horde of new, sleek, venture capital-funded services has arrived on the market peddling what they think is a solution: kits made of raw ingredients &#x2014; portioned and sometimes prepped &#x2014; that can be assembled quickly to make a meal &#x201C;from scratch.&#x201D;\u003Cbr\u003E\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\n\u003Cp\u003EThe rising popularity of these meal kits has led to a Gold Rush of sorts. Big brands like \u003Ca href=\"https:\u002F\u002Fwww.blueapron.com\u002F\"\u003EBlue Apron\u003C\u002Fa\u003E, \u003Ca href=\"https:\u002F\u002Fwww.plated.com\u002F\"\u003EPlated\u003C\u002Fa\u003E, and \u003Ca href=\"https:\u002F\u002Fwww.hellofresh.com\u002F\"\u003EHello Fresh\u003C\u002Fa\u003E cater to the general population, each offering a half dozen or so meal plans for everyone from families to vegetarians. Then there are the niche kits: organic food (\u003Ca href=\"http:\u002F\u002Featpurely.com\u002F\"\u003EEat Purely\u003C\u002Fa\u003E), vegan food (\u003Ca href=\"https:\u002F\u002Fwww.thepurplecarrot.com\u002F\"\u003EThe Purple Carrot\u003C\u002Fa\u003E), Southern cooking (\u003Ca href=\"https:\u002F\u002Fwww.peachdish.com\u002F\"\u003EPeachDish\u003C\u002Fa\u003E), and smoothies (\u003Ca href=\"https:\u002F\u002Fgreenblender.com\u002F\"\u003EGreen Blender\u003C\u002Fa\u003E). All claim to work with local suppliers to some extent, creating a whole new distribution outlet for small- to mid-size farms.\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\n\u003Cp\u003EAlthough these kits have the potential to waste a lot of packaging, many of the companies behind them actually hope to cut down on food waste. Instead of buying obscure ingredients you&#x2019;ll only use once, or receiving three heads of kale in your weekly community supported agriculture (CSA) subscription box that will inevitably wilt in the crisper drawer, the kits provide you with only what you need for a recipe. Not a bad model for a country that throws away \u003Ca href=\"http:\u002F\u002Fcivileats.com\u002F2014\u002F10\u002F07\u002Funcovering-americas-food-waste-fiasco\u002F\"\u003E35 million tons\u003C\u002Fa\u003E of food a year.\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\n\u003Cp\u003E\u003Cb\u003E\u003Ca href=\"http:\u002F\u002Fcivileats.com\u002F2015\u002F06\u002F25\u002Fsearching-for-food-you-can-believe-in-eat-well-guides-new-app-has-you-covered\u002F#sthash.ufXlJDnq.dpuf\"\u003EMore: Searching for Food You Can Believe in? Eat Well Guide&#x2019;s New App Has You Covered&#xA0;\u003C\u002Fa\u003E\u003C\u002Fb\u003E\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\n\u003Cfigure class=\"tmblr-full\"\u003E\n \u003Cimg src=\"https:\u002F\u002Fs.yimg.com\u002Fg\u002Fimages\u002Fspaceball.gif\" alt=\"image\" width=\"540\" height=\"360\" data-src=\"https:\u002F\u002Fs.yimg.com\u002Fcd\u002Fresizer\u002F2.0\u002FFIT_TO_WIDTH-w540\u002Ff54143c1b1ecee723b1ea581f528876397afc086.jpg\"\u003E\n\u003C\u002Ffigure\u003E\n\u003Cp\u003E\u003Ci\u003EAn assortment of meal kits from Blue Apron.\u003C\u002Fi\u003E\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\n\u003Cp\u003ESome meal kit creators also strive to eliminate food waste higher in the supply chain. Blue Apron claims to deliver more than 3 million meals a month. That requires a lot of produce, and Blue Apron and other services are collaborating with farmers, in some cases planning menus a year out in order to sync with crop rotations, and ensure that all the food each farm grows goes to use. In doing so, they could be creating a new form of farm-to-table food delivery, somewhere in between a CSA and a restaurant.\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\n\u003Cp\u003E&#x201C;We&#x2019;ve had a farm strategy since day one,&#x201D; says Matthew Wadiak, founder and COO of Blue Apron. He says that the three-year-old company has spent the past few years talking with farmers, assessing their needs and challenges, then figuring out how to address them. Wadiak is a champion of forgotten heirloom produce, like \u003Ca href=\"http:\u002F\u002Fwww.highmowingseeds.com\u002Forganic-non-gmo-seeds-honey-nut-butternut-squash.html\"\u003Ehoneynut squash\u003C\u002Fa\u003E and \u003Ca href=\"http:\u002F\u002Fblack%20panther%20soybeans\u002F\"\u003Eblack panther soybeans\u003C\u002Fa\u003E, which he says goes over well with both his customers and the farmers.\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\n\u003Cp\u003E\u003Ca href=\"http:\u002F\u002Fcivileats.com\u002F2015\u002F02\u002F12\u002Fis-the-online-grocery-boom-good-for-the-planet\u002F\"\u003E\u003Cb\u003EMore: Is The Online Grocery Boom Good for the Planet?\u003C\u002Fb\u003E\u003C\u002Fa\u003E\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\n\u003Cp\u003EBlue Apron works with the 31 farms, and the culinary staff have sustainable agriculture backgrounds (the culinary director came from \u003Ca href=\"https:\u002F\u002Fwww.stonebarnscenter.org\u002F\"\u003EStone Barns Center for Food and Agriculture\u003C\u002Fa\u003E), so an awareness of crop rotation and cover crops has been built into their business model.\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\n\u003Cp\u003EFor example, the company recently worked with 12-acre Alewife Farm farm and others nearby in New York&#x2019;s Hudson Valley to source thousands of pounds of pea shoots for a recent \u003Ca href=\"https:\u002F\u002Fwww.blueapron.com\u002Frecipes\u002Fseared-wild-king-salmon-with-preserved-lemon-quinoa\"\u003Eseared salmon dish\u003C\u002Fa\u003E. \u003Ca href=\"http:\u002F\u002Fcivileats.com\u002F2014\u002F06\u002F16\u002Fstarting-out-a-new-farmers-first-growing-season\u002F\"\u003EAlewife owner Tyler Dennis\u003C\u002Fa\u003E says that the peas helped fix nitrogen in his soil, and the guaranteed revenue from the order was a huge boon.\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\n\u003Cp\u003E\u003Cb\u003E\u003Ca href=\"http:\u002F\u002Fcivileats.com\u002F2015\u002F02\u002F06\u002Fhow-can-we-get-america-cooking-one-crumb-at-a-time\u002F#sthash.Se8xPhyJ.dpuf\"\u003EMore:&#xA0;How Can We Get America Cooking? One Crumb at a Time\u003C\u002Fa\u003E\u003C\u002Fb\u003E&#xA0;\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\n\u003Cp\u003EFarmers are not only reliant on the weather, but also on the whims of customers at farmers&#x2019; markets and the picky palates of chefs to sell their wares. Dennis is talking with the company to grow more peas, as well as some baby fennel and baby leeks. &#x201C;I would really like to incorporate my business with Blue Apron&#x2019;s in a more substantial way,&#x201D; he says.\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\n\u003Cp\u003EThese meal kits can be expensive when compared to a home-cooked meal at around $8 and $12 per person. That&#x2019;s not much more than take-out from most casual restaurants, but they do require 10-30 minutes of actual cooking time. They also create their own waste in the form of the packaging that holds, say, two tablespoons of butter for one recipe, or the ice packs to keep the food cold. But meal kit proponents are quick to point out that they&#x2019;re also eliminating a lot of the packaging higher up in the food distribution stream.\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\n\u003Cp\u003E\u003Cb\u003EMore: An App for That: Technology as a Solution to Our Broken Food System?&#xA0;\u003C\u002Fb\u003E\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\n\u003Cp\u003EPerhaps the most limiting part, at least to someone who knows how to cook, is that these services only offer a few options each day. That&#x2019;s where a model more like \u003Ca href=\"https:\u002F\u002Flukeslocal.com\u002F\"\u003ELuke&#x2019;s Local\u003C\u002Fa\u003E, a San Francisco-based meal delivery company, comes in. Its stated goal is to help busy people get through the week. So the business offers recipe kits, but also heat-and-serve prepared meals and raw produce and ingredients, more like a regular CSA.\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\n\u003Cp\u003E&#x201C;[Our customers] love that they can get some of these things to cook dinner or have dinner at home, some fruit for the morning for breakfast, a box lunch to bring to work,&#x201D; says owner Luke Chappell.\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\n\u003Cp\u003E\u003Ca href=\"http:\u002F\u002Fcivileats.com\u002F2014\u002F11\u002F17\u002Ftoss-those-take-out-menus-new-study-says-cooking-makes-us-healthier\u002F#sthash.Il10pdyd.dpuf\"\u003E\u003Cb\u003EMore: Toss Those Take-Out Menus: New Study Says Cooking Makes us Healthier\u003C\u002Fb\u003E\u003C\u002Fa\u003E\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\n\u003Cp\u003ELike Wadiak, Chappell has made working with farmers a priority from the beginning. He says that there&#x2019;s rarely a day that goes by without communication between his team of chefs and farmers like Andy Griffin from Watsonville&#x2019;s \u003Ca href=\"http:\u002F\u002Fwww.mariquita.com\u002F\"\u003EMariquita Farm\u003C\u002Fa\u003E&#x2014;either they&#x2019;re on the phone talking about what&#x2019;s fresh that week, or Griffin is texting them photos of what&#x2019;s ripe and good to feature. In a weekly meeting, the team looks at all the produce set to come in and figures out what to do with it.\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\n\u003Cp\u003EOffering a range of options also eliminates waste almost entirely, says Chappell. For example, he can source a whole pig from Chico, California-based \u003Ca href=\"http:\u002F\u002Fllanoseco.com\u002F\"\u003ELlano Seco Ranch\u003C\u002Fa\u003E and use every part: the skin for chicharones, the bones for broth, the cuts for the prepared chefs meals, chorizo for a breakfast burrito, and tenderloins for a dinner recipe kit.\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\n\u003Cp\u003E\u003Ca href=\"http:\u002F\u002Fcivileats.com\u002F2013\u002F10\u002F14\u002Fcooking-as-the-cornerstone-of-a-sustainable-food-system\u002F#sthash.VVJ03odz.dpuf\"\u003E\u003Cb\u003ECooking as the Cornerstone of a Sustainable Food System\u003C\u002Fb\u003E\u003C\u002Fa\u003E&#xA0;\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\n\u003Cp\u003EFood gurus like Michael Pollan and Mark Bittman often point to scratch cooking as \u003Ca href=\"http:\u002F\u002Ftime.com\u002F3483888\u002Fthe-truth-about-home-cooking\u002F\"\u003Ethe answer\u003C\u002Fa\u003E to many of \u003Ca href=\"http:\u002F\u002Fwww.nytimes.com\u002F2009\u002F08\u002F02\u002Fmagazine\u002F02cooking-t.html?pagewanted=all&amp;_r=0\"\u003Eour food system&#x2019;s ills\u003C\u002Fa\u003E, and the best a way to eat sustainably grown ingredients without breaking the bank. But it&#x2019;s unclear whether or not meal kits can ever serve as a bridge to more affordable, traditional home cooking.\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\n\u003Cp\u003EThey could simply be a function of the new &#x201C;\u003Ca href=\"https:\u002F\u002Fmedium.com\u002Fondemand\u002Fthe-shut-in-economy-ec3ec1294816\"\u003Eshut in economy\u003C\u002Fa\u003E,&#x201D; where those with means order everything into their homes and never leave. But those behind the companies say they&#x2019;re working to make it easier for busy professionals and families, who might not cook at all otherwise, to take advantage of the values of community supported agriculture or farmers&#x2019; market shopping without the time commitment.\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\n\u003Cp\u003E&#x201C;My argument is that we take the good parts of the CSA, which is the seasonality, but we make it really usable for everybody,&#x201D; says Wadiak. And no matter how you feel about the cooking-by-the-numbers approach to dinner, it&#x2019;s hard to argue with that.\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\n\u003Cp\u003E\u003Cb\u003EMore food for thought from Yahoo Drinks That Do (and Taste) Good\u003C\u002Fa\u003E\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\n\u003Cp\u003E\u003Ca Women\u003C\u002Fa\u003E\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\n\u003Cp\u003E\u003Ca href=\"https:\u002F\u002Fwww.yahoo.com\u002Ffood\u002Fwhat-its-really-like-to-cook-on-a-food-stamp-122876361359.html\"\u003EWhat
